    "double affine hecke algebras , also known as _ cherednik algebras _ , were first introduced by cherednik as a tool for proving the macdonald constant term conjectures . in @xcite",
    ", the authors introduce a category @xmath0 of modules for a given cherednik algebra , which control the representation theory of the underlying cyclotomic hecke algebra in much the same way as the classical @xmath1-schur algebra does in the case of type @xmath2 .",
    "fix a _ weighting _ @xmath3 , an _",
    "@xmath5 , @xmath6 , and @xmath7 . in @xcite",
    ", webster defines a finite dimensional ( graded ) cellular algebra , @xmath8 , whose module category provides a graded lift of this category @xmath0 .",
    "this algebra is defined by a diagrammatic presentation similar to that of khovanov and lauda , @xcite .",
    "the diagrammatic calculus of this algebra captures a great deal of representation theoretic information . in this paper",
    ", we shall study a certain saturated quotient of webster s algebra in the case that the weighting @xmath9 is such that @xmath10 for all @xmath11 ( we refer to this as a flotw weighting , after @xcite ) . here",
    ", the set of one - column multipartitions , @xmath12 , forms a saturated set ; of principal interest in this paper will be the quotient algebra ( which we call the _ quiver temperley ",
    "lieb algebra of type @xmath13 _ ) whose module category is the subcategory of representations whose simple constituents lie in this saturated set .",
    "strikingly , the elements of webster s cellular basis in this quotient algebra may be indexed by orbits of paths in a euclidean space under the action of an affine weyl group of type @xmath14 . moreover ,",
    "the graded dimensions of the standard modules are given by running a cancellation - free version of soergel s algorithm along the paths in this alcove geometry .",
    "motivated by this example , we introduce the notion of an algebra with a _ soergel - path basis_. in theorem [ main : theorem : general ] , we show that ( under certain assumptions ) the graded decomposition numbers of such an algebra are given by the associated kazhdan  lusztig polynomials .",
    "our approach makes use only of elementary linear algebra and is based on kleshchev and nash s proof of the llt algorithm , @xcite .",
    "in particular , given a cherednik algebra with flotw weighting , the graded decomposition numbers @xmath15 for @xmath16 are given by the affine kazhdan  lusztig polynomials of type @xmath14 ( see corollary [ mainresultforchered ] ) .",
    "it is shown in @xcite that the decomposition numbers of @xmath8 can be equated with coefficients of uglov s canonical basis of a twisted fock space .",
    "therefore the decomposition numbers may , in principle , be calculated by running an analogue of the llt algorithm , see @xcite , but not in terms of kazhdan  lusztig polynomials .",
    "our alcove - geometric description comes complete with a translation principle ; it also allows us to deduce that the decomposition numbers are stable as the rank @xmath17 tends to infinity .",
    "thus , we conjecture that the algebras considered here are asymptotically related ( as the rank tends to infinity ) to affine kac  moody algebras ( see @xcite ) and in finite rank to the _ generalised blob algebras _ ( see @xcite ) . in the level 2 case ,",
    "the blob algebra first arose in the study of two - dimensional potts models , @xcite , and has subsequently been related to the virasoro algebra @xcite in the limit as @xmath17 tends to infinity .    in order to clarify the above ,",
    "let s consider an example .",
    "we will omit technical details and definitions at this stage , and instead concentrate on giving a flavour of the combinatorics that is involved .",
    "let @xmath18 , @xmath19 , @xmath20 , @xmath21 .",
    "we shall consider a single block / linkage class of the algebra @xmath22 .",
    "we embed the one - column multipartitions into euclidean space via the embedding @xmath23 and shall label representations of the algebra by these points ( rather than the multipartitions ) .",
    "these points belong to the codimension 1 hyperplane given by @xmath24 , which is depicted in figure [ 2diag ] , below .",
    "the affine weyl group acts on this space fixing the point @xmath25 for @xmath26 .",

    ", we fix a distinguished path , @xmath36 , from the origin to @xmath32 , and for each @xmath37 in the above set , we look at paths which may be obtained by folding - up the path @xmath36 along hyperplanes so that it terminates at @xmath37 ( as illustrated shortly ) ; we denote the set of such paths by @xmath38 .",
    "each path has an associated degree which can be calculated by running soergel s ( cancellation - free ) algorithm along this path .",
    "the key to working with the quiver temperley ",

    "this is a dual set - up to that usually considered .",
    "as @xmath17 tends to infinity , we find that there are infinitely many @xmath32 such that @xmath43 ; the dimension of the cell module @xmath34 and the number of composition factors of @xmath34 also tend to infinity as @xmath17 becomes arbitrarily large .",

    "suppose that we are not in the case above , then we must apply the relations to the product to obtain a diagram of the form @xmath842 for some @xmath838 .",
    "this product has a number of ` extra crossings ' of strands of the same residue ( that is , crossings which do not appear in @xmath843 ) .",
    "the rightmost of these crossings involves a pair of strands of residue @xmath148 , say .",
    "this crossing is bypassed by the ghost of the strand of residue @xmath844 immediately to its right ( for an example , see figure [ lironsayingrelations ] ) . applying relation ( 2.10 )",
    ", the product can be written as a sum of two terms : one is zero modulo more dominant terms , the other differs from the original diagram only where we have untied the distinguished crossing ( for an example , see figure [ lironsayingrelations ] ) .",
    "now suppose that the resulting diagram is not equal to @xmath843 , in which case it has a rightmost ` extra crossing ' of residue @xmath845 .",
    "now consider the ghost of the leftmost of the two strands we untied in the previous step ; the ghost of this strand bypasses the rightmost ` extra crossing ' .",
    "repeating the above argument for all the crossings , we obtain the result .",
